## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves the relationship between stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which falls squarely in the domain of solid mechanics / materials science constitutive modeling. The stress-strain relationship is fundamental, and temperature dependence introduces thermal softening, thermal activation, and viscoelastic/viscoplastic effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus varying with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain for strain hardening materials)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic stress-strain with hardening)
- Thermal softening with power-law strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T)**c3 (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type (isothermal): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal term)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law hardening with thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-like thermal activation on flow stress)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturating hardening with temperature-dependent saturation stress)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (Taylor expansion of constitutive law)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift equation: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (power-law with pre-strain offset)
- Thermal expansion stress: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress accounting for thermal strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (concave stress-strain curve) → Power-law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturating exponential (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening (decreasing stress with temperature) → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n) or exp(-c*T)
- Yield stress / elastic limit → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon), where c0 represents initial yield
- Stress saturation at large strains → Voce-type form c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)) indicating dislocation saturation
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain and temperature effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable structure common in constitutive models
- Pre-strain or residual strain offset → (epsilon + c0)**c1 form, shifting the strain origin
- Linear thermoelastic regime → sigma proportional to (epsilon - c*T), subtracting thermal expansion strain
- Competing hardening and softening → Sum of increasing function of epsilon and decreasing function of T, e.g., c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*T

### Candidate 16: T·c0·sin(c1+c2·ε) + c3·ε + c4 + c5·exp(c6·ε)·sin(c7·ε+c8)

exp(c6·ε)·sin(c7·ε+c8) cannot equal ε³ + a·sin(ε) + b·ε + d for all ε. These are fundamentally different functions.

**Candidate 17 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 31: T·c0·sin(c1+ε) + c2·ε + c3 + c4·sin(c5·ε+c6)·cos(c7·ε)

c4·sin(c5·ε+c6)·cos(c7·ε): Using product-to-sum: = (c4/2)·[sin((c5+c7)ε+c6) + sin((c5-c7)ε+c6)].

### Candidate 37: T·c0·sin(c1+ε) + c2·ε + c3·ε³ + c4·sin(c5+c6·ε)
Set c1=0: T·c0·sin(ε). ✓
c3·ε³ ✓
c4·sin(c5+c6·ε): set c6=1, c5=0: c4·sin(ε). ✓
c2·ε: set c2=0. ✓

So: T·c0·sin(ε) + c3·ε³ + c4·sin(ε) = c0·T·sin(ε) + c3·ε³ + c4·sin(ε)

GT = c_b·T·sin(ε) - c_b·c_3·sin(ε) + c_a·ε³

This matches! Set c0 = c_b = 2.882..., c3 = 5.889..., c4 = -c_b·c_3 = -2.882...×279.62... = -806.2..., c2 = 0, c1 = 0.

**Candidate 37 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 40: (c0·ε+c1+(T·c2+c3)·(T·c4·sin(c5+ε)+c6·ε+c7·ε³))/(T·c2+c3)
= (c0·ε+c1)/(T·c2+c3) + T·c4·sin(c5+ε) + c6·ε + c7·ε³

The first term (c0·ε+c1)/(T·c2+c3) is a rational function of T. Set c0=0, c1=0: T·c4·sin(c5+ε) + c6·ε + c7·ε³.

Set c5=0: T·c4·sin(ε) + c6·ε + c7·ε³. Need sin(ε) term too. GT has sin(ε) standalone. Here we only have T·sin(ε), ε, ε³. Set c6=0: T·c4·sin(ε) + c7·ε³. Missing the sin(ε) term.

What if c0≠0 or c1≠0? Then (c0·ε+c1)/(T·c2+c3) introduces T-dependent rational terms. For this to give a·sin(ε), it can't since it's rational in ε.

Actually wait - can we use the first term? (c0·ε+c1)/(T·c2+c3) = c0·ε/(T·c2+c3) + c1/(T·c2+c3). These are not sin(ε). So no way to get the standalone sin(ε) term.

**Candidate 40 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

c5·ε³ ✓

### Candidate 48: (T·c0+c1+(c2·ε+c3)·(T·c4·sin(c5+ε)+c6·ε+c7·ε³))/(c2·ε+c3)

Actually, what if c2=0? Then (T·c0+c1)/c3 + T·c4·sin(c5+ε) + c6·ε + c7·ε³ = T·c0/c3 + c1/c3 + T·c4·sin(c5+ε) + c6·ε + c7·ε³.

Wait, with c2=0 and c0=0: (c1 + c3·(T·c4·sin(c5+ε) + c6·ε + c7·ε³))/c3 = c1/c3 + T·c4·sin(c5+ε) + c6·ε + c7·ε³. No standalone sin(ε).

**Candidate 48 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 58: T·c0·sin(c1·ε+c2) + T·c3·sin(c4+ε) + c5·ε + c6·ε³

## Summary

Only Candidate 37 matches: T·c0·sin(c1+ε) + c2·ε + c3·ε³ + c4·sin(c5+c6·ε)

With c1=0, c6=1, c5=0, c2=0: T·c0·sin(ε) + c3·ε³ + c4·sin(ε) = c0·T·sin(ε) + c4·sin(ε) + c3·ε³

This exactly matches GT = c_b·T·sin(ε) + c_a·ε³ - c_b·c_3·sin(ε).
